<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-indent: -0.5in; text-align: center;"><a name="OLE_LINK11"></a><a name="OLE_LINK13"></a><a name="OLE_LINK6"></a><a name="OLE_LINK5"></a><a name="OLE_LINK4"></a><span style="font-size: 18pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino; color: #ffffff; background-color: #808080;"><b><span style="line-height: 115%; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;">Spiritual (Festival) Message for the Day  Skanda Sashti by Gurudev Sri Swami Sivananda</span></b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-indent: -0.5in; text-align: center;">&nbsp;<strong style="text-indent: -0.5in;"><span style="font-family: book antiqua,palatino; font-size: 12pt; color: #3366ff;"><span style="line-height: 115%;"><span style="color: #0000ff;">Baba Times Digest | 17 November 2015 18</span></span></span></strong><strong style="text-indent: -0.5in;"><span style="font-family: book antiqua,palatino; font-size: 12pt; color: #3366ff;"><span style="line-height: 115%;"><span style="color: #0000ff;">.58 EST | New York Edition</span></span></span></strong></p>
<hr />
<div>
<table cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" hspace="0" vspace="0" align="left">
<tbody>
<tr>
<td valign="top" align="left" style="padding-top: 0in; padding-right: 9.0pt; padding-bottom: 0in; padding-left: 9.0pt;">
<p align="center" style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: center; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><b>Skanda Sashti</b><o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p align="center" style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: center; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><b>Divine Life Society Publication:<span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></b><a href="http://www.dlshq.org/religions/skanda.htm" target="_blank"><b><span style="color: #1155cc;">Hindu Fasts and Festivals</span></b></a><span class="apple-converted-space"><b>&nbsp;</b></span><b>by<span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></b><a href="http://www.dlshq.org/saints/siva.htm" target="_blank"><b><span style="color: #1155cc;">Gurudev Sri Swami Sivananda</span></b></a><o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p align="center" style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: center; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><b><span style="color: #1155cc;">&nbsp;</span></b></span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">PROSTRATIONS and humble salutations to Lord Subramanya, the Supreme Being, who is the ruler of this universe, who is the indweller of our hearts, who is the second son of Lord Siva, who is the beloved of Valli and Deivayanai, who bestows boons easily on His devotees, who is the embodiment of power, wisdom, love and bliss.<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Lord Subramanya is an incarnation of Lord Siva. All incarnations are manifestations of the one Supreme Lord. Lord Subramanya and Lord Krishna are one.<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Lord Krishna says in the<span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span>Gita:<span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span>"Among the army generals, I am Skanda".<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">The Lord manifests Himself from time to time in various names and forms, for the sake of establishing righteousness and subduing wickedness.<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Lord Subramanya is a ray born of the Divine Consciousness of Lord Siva. Valli and Deivayanai are His two wives. They represent the power of action and the power of knowledge respectively. He is a Godhead easily accessible in this dark age of ignorance and lack of faith. In this He is no different from Hanuman. He gives material and spiritual prosperity and success in every undertaking of His devotees, even if they show a little devotion to Him. He is worshipped with great devotion in South India. Lord Subramanya's other names are Kumaresa, Kartikeya, Shanmukha, Guha, Muruga and Velayudhan.<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">In His picture, Lord Subramanya holds a spear in His hand, just as Lord Siva holds the trident. This is an emblem of power. It indicates that He is the ruler of the universe. His vehicle is the peacock. He rides on it. This signifies that He has conquered pride, egoism and vanity. There is a cobra under His feet, which indicates that He is absolutely fearless, immortal and wise. Valli is on His one side, Deivayanai on the other. Sometimes He stands alone with His spear. In this pose He is known as Velayudhan; this is His Nirguna aspect, which is free from the illusory power of Maya.<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">The six heads represent the six rays or attributes, namely, wisdom, dispassion, strength, fame, wealth and divine powers. They indicate that He is the source of the four<span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span>Vedas,<span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span>the<span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span>Vedangas<span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span>and the six schools of philosophy. They also indicate His control over the five organs of knowledge as well as the mind. They denote that He is the Supreme Being with thousands of heads and hands. His head turned in all directions signifies that He is all-pervading. It indicates that He can multiply and assume forms at will.<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Lord Subramanya's temples can be seen in Udipi, in Tiruchendur, in the Palani Hills, in Ceylon, and in Tiruparankundrum. Lord Subramanya spent His days of childhood in Tiruchendur and attained Mahasamadhi at Kathirgamam. If you go to Kathirgamam with faith, devotion and piety, and stay in the temple there for two or three days, the Lord will grant you His vision. You will get rich spiritual experiences. A huge festival is held in the temple every year on Skanda Sashti. Thousands of people visit the place. Massive amounts of camphor are burnt on this occasion.<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Skanda Sashti falls in November. It is the day on which Lord Subramanya defeated the demon Taraka. On this day elaborate festivals are held with great pomp and grandeur. Devotees organise Bhajan and Kirtan programs on a grand scale. Thousands are fed sumptuously. Many incurable diseases are cured if one visits Palani and worships Lord Subramanya there. In South India, the Lord's Lilas are dramatized on the stage.<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">In addition to the Skanda Sashti, devotees of Lord Subramanya observe weekly and monthly days in His honour. Every<span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span><span class="aqj"><span style="z-index: -1;"><span data-term="goog_402500818" tabindex="0" style="z-index: 0;">Friday</span></span></span>, or the Kartigai Nakshatram day every month, or the sixth day of the bright fortnight,--all these are sacred days for His devotees. The sixth day of the month of Tulam (October-November) is the most auspicious of them all. This is the Skanda Sashti day.<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">In many places the festival commences six days prior to the Sashti itself and concludes on the day of the Sashti. During these days, devotees recite various inspiring hymns and read stories connected with Lord Subramanya. They worship the Lord and take Kavadi. They go on pilgrimage to the various Subramanya shrines.<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">The<span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span>Tirumurukatrupadai<span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span>has been composed in His praise by the famous Nakkerar. He who studies this eminent work daily with devotion and faith, gets certain success in life as well as peace and prosperity. The<span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span>Tiruppugal<span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span>is another well-known book in Tamil, which contains the inspiring devotional songs of Arunagirinathar in praise of Lord Subramanya. The<span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span>Kavadichindu<span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span>songs are also in praise of the Lord. The<span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span>Skanda Sashti Kavacham<span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span>is another famous hymn in praise of Lord Subramanya and is sung particularly on festive occasions.<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><span style="text-decoration: underline;">At the Sivananda Ashram in India</span>, Skanda Sashti is observed for six days, preceding and including the Sashti day. Devotees of Lord Subramanya live on milk and fruit and do rigorous Sadhana. They get up at<span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span><span class="aqj"><span style="z-index: -1;"><span data-term="goog_402500819" tabindex="0" style="z-index: 0;">4am</span></span></span><span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span>during Brahmamuhurta and meditate on the Lord.<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">On each of the six days, all the participants do Japa of the Mantra,<span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span>Om Saravanabhavaya Namah,<span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span>as much as possible. They even greet one another with this Mantra.<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Yogis and learned scholars deliver lectures on Subramanya Tattwa, or the divine sport of the Lord. During the evening Satsang, hymns in praise of Lord Subramanya are sung. Readings are taken from my book,<span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span>Lord Shanmukha and His Worship.<span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span>Devotees sing inspiring songs on the Lord.<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">An elaborate ceremonial worship is performed daily to the sacred image of Lord Subramanya. On the last day a grand<span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span>havan<span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span>is performed. The evening Satsang is devoted entirely to the adoration of Lord Subramanya.<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Pray from the bottom of your heart: "O my Lord Subramanya, O all-merciful Lord, I have neither faith nor devotion. I do not know how to worship Thee in the proper manner, or to meditate on Thee. I am Thy child who has lost his way, forgotten the goal and Thy Name. Is it not Thy duty, O compassionate Father, to take me back? O Mother Valli, will you not introduce me to Thy Lord? Thy love for Thy children is deeper and truer than that of anyone else in this world. Though I have become Thy worthless and undutiful child, O beloved Mother Valli, pardon me! Make me dutiful and faithful. I am Thine from this very second; always Thine. All is Thine. It is the Mother's duty to correct, educate and mould Her reckless child when it strays aimlessly on the wrong path. Remove the gulf or the veil of delusion that separates me from Thee. Bless me. Enlighten me. Take me back to Thy holy feet. I have nothing more to say. This is my fervent prayer to Thee and Thy Lord, my beloved and ancient Parents."<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">May Lord Subramanya shower His Grace upon you! May His blessings grant you peace, bliss and prosperity!<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">&nbsp;</span></p>
<p style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: justify; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><b><span style="background: yellow;">Note: Skanda Sashti celebrations in Sivananda Ashram <span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;<span data-term="goog_402500820" tabindex="0" style="z-index: 0;"></span><span class="aqj"><span style="z-index: -1;">November 17,2015</span></span></span></span></b><o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" align="center" style="text-align: center;">&nbsp;</p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><b>Excerpts from: Skanda Sashti <span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></b><a href="http://www.dlshq.org/religions/skanda.htm" target="_blank"><b><span style="color: #1155cc;">Hindu Fasts and Festivals</span></b></a><span class="apple-converted-space"><b>&nbsp;</b></span><b>by<span class="apple-converted-space">&nbsp;</span></b><a href="http://www.dlshq.org/saints/siva.htm" target="_blank"><b><span style="color: #1155cc;">Gurudev Sri Swami Sivananda</span></b></a></span><o:p></o:p></p>

</table>
</div>
